Imprisoning the Refuser in Qasama
States the ruling on imprisonment for refusing to swear in qasama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a person who refuses to swear in qasama is imprisoned until he swears, and explain the legal reasoning behind this enforcement.

Core Idea
Refusal to swear in qasama triggers imprisonment to enforce the heirs' right to oaths.

In the Hanafi school, qasama is a procedure for swearing oaths in murder cases where evidence is lacking. If any individual from the quarter required to participate refuses to swear, the judge does not simply drop the case; instead, he imprisons the refuser until he complies. This lesson examines that ruling and the reasoning that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the refusal of an oath in qasama. The ruling is that the refuser is imprisoned until he swears. Note that this is not simply a fine or dismissal.
2
Understand the context of qasama
Qasama involves 50 oaths shared among the people of the quarter where a murder is found. Their collective oath either exonerates them or points to liability. Each individual's participation is necessary to complete the process.
3
Recognize the legal reasoning
The heirs of the victim have a right that the oaths be taken. Refusal frustrates this right. Imprisonment is a coercive measure to compel fulfillment of the obligation.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi’i) may not imprison but instead take refusal as a basis to impose diya directly. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ابى واحد منهم حبس حتى يحلف [۲۴۱۲] (۵) اگر اہل محلہ میں سے کسی ایک نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو اس کوقید کیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ قسم کھالے۔ محلہ والوں میں سے کوئی قسم کھانے سے انکار کرتا ہے تو اس وقت تک قید کر لیا جائے گا جب تک کہ قسم نہ کھائے۔ گا۔ محلہ میں قتل ہونے کی وجہ سے مقتول کے وارثین کا حق ہو گیا کہ اہل محلہ کو تم کھلائے ۔ اس لئے اگر وہ قسم نہیں کھاتا ہے تو اس کو قید کیا جائے
And if one of them refuses, he is imprisoned until he swears [2412]. (5) If one of the people of the quarter refuses to swear, he will be imprisoned until he swears. When any of the quarter refuses to swear, he is imprisoned until he swears. Because due to the murder in the quarter, the heirs of the victim have a right that the people of the quarter swear. So if he does not swear, he is imprisoned.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This is a ruling on enforcement in qasama. If any individual from the quarter (who is required to participate in the 50 oaths) refuses to swear, the judge imprisons him until he complies. The reasoning is that the heirs of the victim have a right to have the oaths taken, and refusal frustrates that right. Imprisonment is a coercive measure to ensure the procedure is completed.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): Imprisonment as a coercive measure to compel an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a person from the quarter who refuses to swear in a qasama case according to the Hanafi school?
A) The case is dismissed
B) He is imprisoned until he swears
C) Diya is taken from him directly
D) He is fined

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, refusal to swear in qasama leads to imprisonment to enforce the oath, ensuring the heirs' right is fulfilled.

Ruling on Repeating Oaths When Fifty Men Are Not Available
States that if fewer than fifty men are available, oaths are repeated on them to complete fifty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule for completing fifty oaths in qasama by repeating them on available men, and apply it to a given number of men.

Core Idea
In qasama, fifty oaths are required; if fewer men are available, oaths are repeated on them until fifty is reached.

In cases of qasama (collective oath for blood money), the Hanafi school requires fifty oaths. But what if the suspect's quarter has fewer than fifty eligible men? This rule clarifies that the requirement is fifty oaths, not fifty distinct individuals, so oaths are repeated as needed. We'll examine the ruling, its evidence from the early authorities, and how to apply it practically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the qasama procedure requires fifty oaths, but the quarter may have fewer than fifty eligible men. The question is whether the number of men must be fifty or the oaths must total fifty.
The core issue: oaths vs. individuals.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text states: 'If there are not fifty from the people of the quarter, then oaths are repeated upon them until fifty oaths are completed.' This means the total oaths, not men, must be fifty.
Ruling: repeat oaths on the same men to reach fifty.
3
Identify the evidence (dalil)
The ruling is supported by an athar (statement) of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'If they do not complete fifty, then oaths are repeated upon them.' This is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
It is a mursal athar, accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If the quarter has only 10 men, each man swears 5 times to reach 50 oaths. If 20 men, each swears 2.5 times? But oaths are indivisible; the text implies repetition until the count of fifty is achieved, which may require some men to swear one more time than others.
Practical application: total oaths fixed at 50.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لم داؤد شریف [؟] [۲۴۱۲] (٦) اگر اہل محلہ میں سے پچاس پورے نہ ہوں تو ان پر قسم مکرر کی جائے گی۔ یہاں تک کہ پچاس قسمیں پوری ہو جائے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال اذا لم يكملوا خمسين رددت الايمان عليهم (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، با القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۱۱، نمبر ۱۸۲۸۵ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۶۷ ماجاء فی القسامة ج خامس، ص، ۴۴۰، نمبر ۲۷۸۰۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پچاس حاشیہ : (ب) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا اگر پچاس پورے نہ ہوں تو انہیں سے دوبارہ قسم کی جائے۔
And if [the number] is not complete [?] [2412] (6) If there are not fifty from the people of the quarter, then oaths are repeated upon them until fifty oaths are completed. There is an athar: Ibrahim said: 'If they do not complete fifty, then oaths are repeated upon them.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book of Qasama, vol. 10, p. 411, no. 18285; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 27803). From this athar it is understood that fifty [oaths are required]. Footnote (b): Ibrahim said: If fifty are not complete, then oaths are repeated from them.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This ruling addresses the situation when the quarter has fewer than fifty eligible men (e.g., due to small population). The oaths are then repeated on the available men until the total number of oaths reaches fifty. For example, if only ten men are available, each swears five times. The proof is the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, which is recorded in the authoritative collections. This ensures that the requirement of fifty oaths is met regardless of the number of men.

Key Terms
ردت الايمان (ruddat al-ayman): Oaths are repeated or returned to the same individuals to reach the required number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of oaths required in Hanafi qasama?
A) It depends on the number of men available.
B) Thirty oaths, as per general procedure.
C) Fifty oaths, regardless of the number of men.
D) One oath per man, up to fifty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qasama, the fixed requirement is fifty oaths; scarcity of men triggers repetition, not reduction.

Exclusion of Four Categories from Qasama
States exclusion of four categories from qasama with proof from Thawri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories excluded from qasama in the Hanafi school and explain the legal basis from the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri.

Core Idea
Only free, sane, adult males participate in qasama; all others are excluded due to legal incapacity.

The qasama oath is a solemn procedure for resolving disputed blood money claims, but not every resident may swear. This lesson clarifies who is excluded based on the clear statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, which the Hanafi school adopts as a transmitted proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is participation in qasama. The ruling excludes four categories: minors, insane persons, women, and slaves.
The ruling is a declaratory (hukm wad'i) stating legal incapacity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar (statement) of Sufyan al-Thawri, as cited in the commentary: he explicitly excludes women, children, and slaves.
The source mentions two narrations: one excluding women and children, another excluding slaves.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit Arabic phrase 'لا يدخل' (do not enter) indicates a prohibition of inclusion, so these individuals cannot take the oath.
The wording is clear and unequivocal.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may allow women or slaves under certain conditions, but the Hanafi school firmly excludes all four based on this athar.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school follows this athar because it is a transmitted precedent from a reliable early authority, and it aligns with the school's view of legal capacity (ahliyyah).
The mufta bihi is the exclusion of all four categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكمل اهل المحلة كررت الايمان عليهم حتى يتم حتى يتم خمسين يمينا [ ٢۴١٣] (۷) ولا يدخل في القسامة صبى ولا مجنون ولا امرأة ولا عبد [۲۴۱۴] اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچہ عورت، مجنون اور غلام سے قسامت میں قسم کی جائے گی۔ (الف) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا عورتوں اور بچوں پر قسامہ نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ غلام پر قسامہ نہیں ہے
The people of the quarter are completed; oaths are repeated upon them until fifty oaths are completed [2413]. (7) A minor, an insane person, a woman, and a slave are not included in qasama [2414]. From this athar it is understood that a child, a woman, an insane person, and a slave are not sworn in qasama. (a) Thawri said: There is no qasama upon women and children. And in another narration: There is no qasama upon slaves.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This ruling specifies who is eligible to participate in the qasama oath. Only free, sane, adult males qualify. Children lack legal capacity, the insane lack sanity, women are not considered capable of bearing the financial liability of diya (as they may not be able to contribute), and slaves lack property (their assets belong to their master). The proof is the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, who explicitly excludes these categories.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasama): The oath procedure; those excluded cannot swear.
صبى (sabi): Minor child, under the age of legal majority.
مجنون (majnun): Insane person, lacking mental capacity.
امرأة (imra'a): Adult woman.
عبد (abd): Slave, owned by another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is allowed to participate in qasama according to the Hanafi school?
A) A minor boy
B) A slave
C) A free adult man
D) A woman

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school excludes minors, the insane, women, and slaves from qasama, relying on the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri.

Ruling on No Qasama or Diya When No Trace of Violence Found
States that if a dead body is found without any mark of violence, there is no qasama or diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for qasama and apply it to a scenario where a body is found without visible marks.

Core Idea
No trace of violence means no qasama or diya — the quarter is not liable.

This lesson explores a key condition for the application of qasama and diya in Hanafi law. When a dead body is found without any outward sign of injury, the legal presumption shifts away from community liability. We will examine the ruling and its supporting evidence from the early Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that the passage states a negative ruling: no qasama and no diya when no trace (athar) of violence is found on the body.
The ruling is a condition (shart) for liability.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar (statement) from Sufyan al-Thawri, a prominent early authority. It distinguishes between a body with a trace (then 'aql/diya is due) and without (then no liability unless evidence points to a specific person).
The athar is considered a mursal hadith, so its thubut is zanni, but it is relied upon here.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit distinction in the athar shows that the presence of a visible mark of violence is the operative cause (illa) for imposing qasama. Without it, the default is no liability.
This is a straightforward dalala – the text explicitly contrasts the two cases.
4
Check for intra-Hanafi disagreement
The source indicates no disagreement among the Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on this point. The ruling is muttafaq alayh within the school.
Thus, the mufta bihi is clear.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Practice applying the ruling: if a body is found in a town with no wounds, the community is not liable. If a small cut is found, qasama becomes applicable.
This condition protects communities from being held responsible for natural deaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد میت لااثر به فلا قسامة ولا دية [۲۴۱۴] اثر میں ہے۔ عن الثوري قال اذا وجد القتيل فـي قـوم به اثر كان عقله عليهم واذا لم يكن به اثر لم يكن على العاقلة شيء الا ان تقوم البينة على احد (ب) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۰ ، نمبر ۱۸۲۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کر قتل کا اثر نہ ہو تو قسامہ نہیں ہے۔
And if a dead body is found with no trace (of violence), then there is no qasama and no diya [2414]. There is an athar: Thawri said: 'If a killed person is found among a people and there is a trace (of violence), then his 'aql (diya) is upon them; if there is no trace, then nothing is upon the 'aqila unless evidence is established against someone.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book of Qasama, vol. 10, p. 40, no. 18282). From this athar it is understood that if there is no trace of murder, there is no qasama.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This ruling establishes a condition for qasama: there must be a visible sign of violence (e.g., a wound, blood, etc.) on the body. If the body shows no external mark of injury, it is presumed that the death was natural, and thus the quarter is not liable. The proof is the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, who differentiates between a body with a trace (requiring diya from the community) and one without (no liability unless a specific culprit is proven).

Key Terms
أثر (athar): A visible mark of violence (wound, blood, etc.) on the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for qasama to be imposed?
A) The body must be found in a quarter
B) There must be a visible trace of violence on the body
C) The death must occur at night
D) The wali must demand qasama

Key Takeaway
The presence of a visible trace of violence on the body is a necessary condition for qasama and diya in Hanafi law.

Diyah on Driver's Aqilah When Slain Found on Animal
Ruling on liability when a slain body is found on a driven animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that apparent evidence (zahir al-'alamah) determines liability for diyah in cases of unintended homicide, using the athar of Shurayh as proof.

Core Idea
Apparent evidence shifts liability from the neighborhood to the driver's aqilah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter of qasamah: when a slain body is found on an animal being driven, who bears the blood money? The Hanafi school rules that the apparent circumstantial evidence points to the driver, so his 'aqilah is liable. This ruling illustrates how strong circumstantial evidence can establish liability even without direct witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the Arabic text: if a slain is found on an animal being driven, diyah is on the driver's 'aqilah, not the neighborhood. This applies to cases where the killer is not directly witnessed but apparent evidence exists.
The ruling is from the chapter on qasamah.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that apparent signs (zahir al-'alamah) determine liability. Here, the driver's control over the animal makes him the apparent killer.
This principle is used in other areas of fiqh, e.g., finding a corpse on one's property.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites an athar from Shurayh: when a body with no wound was found at a door, he administered oaths to the people of the house. This shows that the place where the body is found determines who is held accountable.
The athar is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Examine the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is derived by analogy: just as the people of the house are tasked with oaths in the athar, the driver is the one whose 'aqilah pays diyah because he is the apparent responsible party.
The illa (effective cause) is the apparent connection to the death.
5
Note the practical effect on qasamah
Once the apparent killer is identified, the neighborhood is no longer required to perform qasamah. The liability is fixed on the driver's 'aqilah.
This narrows the burden from the community to a specific individual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وجد القتيل على دابة يسوقها رجل فالدية على عاقلته دون اهل المحلة۔ اگر مقتول کسی سواری پر ہو جس کو ایک آدمی ہانک رہا ہو تو دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہے نہ کہ محلہ والے پر۔ یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ ظاہر علامت سے جو قاتل نظر آتا ہو دیت یا قسامت اسی پر ہے۔ یہاں سواری پر لاش ہے اور آدمی اس کو ہانک بھی رہا ہے تو ظاہری علامت یہی ہے کہ یہی اس کا قاتل ہے۔ اس لئے جانور والے پر ہی دیت ہوگی اور قاتل کا پتا چل گیا تو اہل محلہ سے قسامت ساقط ہو جائے گی (۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ قال اتى شريح في رجل وجد ميتا على دكان بباب قوم ليس فيه اثر فاستحلف اهل البيت (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۴ نمبر ۱۸۲۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کسی کے دروازے پر لاش پائی جائے تو اس گھر والے کو تم کھلائی جائے گی ۔ اسی طرح کسی کی سواری پر لاش پائی جائے تو اس پر اس کی دیت لازم ہوگی۔
And if the slain is found on an animal being driven by a man, then the blood money is on his 'aqilah, not the people of the neighborhood. If the slain is on a mount being driven by a man, the blood money is on his 'aqilah, not the people of the neighborhood. This issue is based on the principle that from the apparent sign, whoever appears to be the killer, the blood money or qasamah is upon him. Here, the corpse is on the mount and the man is driving it, so the apparent sign is that he is the killer. Therefore, the blood money is on the owner of the animal, and since the killer is identified, qasamah from the people of the neighborhood drops. (2) There is an indication of this in an athar: He said, 'Shurayh was approached regarding a man who found a dead body on a bench at the door of some people, and there was no wound on it, so he administered an oath to the people of the house.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, volume 10, p. 44, no. 18295). From this athar, it is understood that if a corpse is found at someone's door, the people of the house are administered an oath. Similarly, if a corpse is found on someone's mount, then the blood money is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter of Qasamah. It states that if a slain body is found on an animal being driven by a man, the blood money (diyah) is on the 'aqilah of the driver, not on the people of the neighborhood. The reasoning is that the apparent evidence (zahir al-‘alamah) points to the driver as the killer because he is in control of the animal. Once the apparent killer is identified, qasamah (oaths) from the neighborhood is dropped. The author then cites an athar from Shurayh to support the principle that apparent evidence determines liability. In the athar, when a body with no wounds was found at a door, Shurayh administered oaths to the people of the house. This indicates that the place where the body is found determines liability. Similarly, the driver is treated as the apparent killer. The ruling is based on the principle that strong circumstantial evidence can establish liability in homicide cases where direct evidence is lacking.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (‘āqilah): The paternal relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying diyah in cases of unintended homicide.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of the victim as compensation for homicide.
قسامت (qasāmah): A procedure of oaths administered to establish liability when the killer is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ruling in this lesson, if a slain body is found on a donkey being driven by a man, who is liable for the diyah?
A) The man driving the donkey
B) The people of the neighborhood
C) The owner of the donkey
D) The 'aqilah of the man driving

Key Takeaway
Apparent circumstantial evidence can determine liability for diyah in Hanafi fiqh, shifting the burden from the community to the individual identified by the evidence.

Qasamah and Diyah for House Owner
Ruling with proof: house owner liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qasamah is wajib on the house owner and diyah on his 'aqilah when a complete body is found inside, and identify the condition that the body must be whole.

Core Idea
Finding a complete corpse in a house makes the owner liable for qasamah and diyah on his 'aqilah.

This lesson examines a specific case of qasamah (oaths) and diyah (blood money) when a slain body is discovered inside a private dwelling. The Hanafi position relies on strong circumstantial evidence: the location of the body points to the owner as the killer. We will also explore an essential condition from the evidence – the body must be complete for liability to attach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Finding a slain body in a house. What is the legal consequence? Qasamah is wajib on the house owner, diyah on his 'aqilah.
The ruling is conditional on the body being complete.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is an athar from al-Sha'bi transmitted in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. Identify the source and its chain (Sunnah ahad).
This is a zanni al-thubut dalil.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the athar prove the ruling? It states that if the body (badan) is found in a house, funeral prayer is performed and blood money is paid. The location triggers liability. Conversely, if only a part (head or leg) is found, neither applies. The operative phrase is 'body' – indicating completeness.
The condition of completeness is derived from the contrast between 'badan' and 'ra's aw rijl'.
4
Apply the ruling to the case
The author concludes that when the entire corpse is found, the owner bears qasamah and diyah because the apparent sign (zahir) points to him, not neighbors. The killing is treated as khatā’ (unintentional), so diyah falls on the 'aqilah.
The mufta bihi position is as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد القتيل فى دار انسان فالقسامة عليه والدية على عاقلته۔ اگر مقتول پایا گیا کسی انسان کے گھر میں تو قسامت گھر والے پر ہے اور دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہے۔ جب اس کے گھر میں لاش پائی گئی تو ظاہری علامت یہی ہے کہ اسی نے مارا ہے، محلے والے نے نہیں مارا ہے۔ اس لئے اسی پر قسامت ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ قتل خطاء کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے اس کے عاقلہ پر دیت لازم ہوگی (۲) عن الشعبي قال اذا وجد بدن القتيل في دار او مكان صلى عليه وعقل واذا وجد رأس او رجل لم يصل عليه ولم يعقل (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۴ نمبر ۱۸۲۹۶) اس اثر سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ جس کے گھر میں لاش پائی جائے دیت اس پر لازم ہوگی۔ اور دوسری بات یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ نماز پڑھنے وغیرہ میں بدن کا اعتبار ہے کہ بدن ملے تو لازم ہوگی۔ صرف سر ہو یا صرف ٹانگ ہو تو اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ اصل آدمی نہیں ہے صرف ایک ٹکڑا ہے۔
And if the slain is found in a man's house, then qasamah is upon him and the blood money is on his 'aqilah. If the slain is found in someone's house, then qasamah is on the householder and the blood money is on his 'aqilah. When the corpse is found in his house, the apparent sign is that he killed him, not the people of the neighborhood. Therefore, qasamah is upon him. And since the killing is in the category of unintentional (khatā’), the blood money is obligatory on his 'aqilah. (2) From al-Sha'bi, he said: 'If the body of the slain is found in a house or place, funeral prayer is performed for him and blood money is paid. If only the head or a leg is found, funeral prayer is not performed for him and blood money is not paid.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 44, no. 18296). From this athar, two things are understood: first, that whoever's house the corpse is found in, the blood money is obligatory upon him; second, that for funeral prayer and other matters, consideration is given to the body—if the body is found, it is obligatory; if only the head or leg is found, funeral prayer is not performed for him because it is not the actual person but just a piece.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling when a slain body is found inside a house. The owner of the house is subject to qasamah (oaths) and his 'aqilah must pay diyah. The reasoning is that the location of the body provides strong circumstantial evidence that the owner is the killer, not the neighbors. The killing is treated as unintentional (khatā’) for diyah purposes, so the 'aqilah pays. The author then cites an athar from al-Sha'bi which adds two points: first, that finding the body in the house triggers both funeral prayer and blood money; second, that if only a part like the head or leg is found, neither applies, because the body must be complete to be considered the victim. This underscores that the ruling applies specifically to a complete corpse found within the premises.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasāma): Oaths of innocence taken by a person suspected of homicide, typically 50 oaths.
عاقلة (ʻāqila): Blood money paying group (tribal or professional guarantors) that pays diyah on behalf of the killer.
دية (diya): Blood money: financial compensation for wrongful death, paid to the victim's heirs.
قتل خطاء (qatl khaṭā’): Unintentional homicide, where the killer did not intend to kill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the athar from al-Sha'bi, what is the ruling if only a part of the body (e.g., a leg) is found in a house?
A) Funeral prayer is performed and blood money is paid
B) Funeral prayer is performed but no blood money
C) Neither funeral prayer nor blood money
D) Blood money is paid but no funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that finding a complete corpse in a house imposes qasamah on the owner and diyah on his 'aqilah, based on circumstantial evidence and the athar of al-Sha'bi.

Tenants Excluded from Qasamah with Owners: Abu Hanifah's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether tenants participate in qasamah with owners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifah's and Abu Yusuf's positions on who is liable for qasamah and apply the mufta bihi view to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Only original landowners (ahl al-khattah) are liable for qasamah, not tenants or later buyers.

The Hanafi school recognizes a dispute between its founding imams on the scope of qasamah liability. While Abu Hanifah restricts it to the original landowners granted at conquest, Abu Yusuf extends it to all residents including tenants and buyers. Understanding this difference is crucial for correctly applying qasamah when a body is found. This lesson examines their proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifah's position
Identify the ruling that only original landowners (ahl al-khattah) are subject to qasamah; tenants and buyers are excluded.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that all residents—original owners, tenants, and buyers—must take the oath.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's evidence: the practice at Khaybar where the Prophet (ﷺ) made the Jewish residents—who were tenants after conquest—swear oaths.
Abu Yusuf argues that if even non-owners were made to swear, then tenants and buyers should also be liable.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand that Abu Hanifah's response likely distinguishes the Khaybar case as a specific situation (khusus) or notes that the Jews were not merely tenants but had a different status.
The exact rebuttal is not detailed here, but the principle is that qasamah attaches to permanent ownership.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Realize the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifah, only the original owner(s) swear; under Abu Yusuf, all residents swear, increasing the pool of oath-takers.
This affects the probability of proof in a murder case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يدخل السكان في القسامة مع الملاك عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله۔ اور قسامت اہل خطہ پر ہوگی نہ کہ خریداروں پر اگر چہ ان میں سے ایک ہی باقی ہو۔ تش امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جو لوگ زمین کے اصل مالک ہیں یعنی ملک فتح کے وقت حاکم نے جن جن کو لکھ کر زمین حوالہ کیا ہے انہیں لوگوں قسامت لی جائے گی۔ جو لوگ کرایہ پر گھر لئے ہیں یا زمین کو خرید کر رہتے ہیں ان لوگوں سے قسامت نہیں لی جائے گی چاہے اصل مالک ایک ہی ہو اسی سے قسامت لی جائے گی۔ نانی امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کرایہ دار یا بعد میں زمین خرید کر رہنے والے اور اصل مالک سب سے قسامت لی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ بھی قتل میں شریک ہو سکتے ہیں۔ یا سب کو قتل کرنے والوں کی معلومات ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس لئے محلے میں رہنے والے سبھی سے قسم لی جائے گی (۲) اہل خیبر کے یہودیوں سے قسم لی تو ان میں اصل مالک اور کرایہ دار کا فرق نہیں کیا بلکہ سب سے قسم لی۔ یوں بھی اس وقت وہ لوگ اصل مالک نہیں تھے۔ کیونکہ خیبر فتح ہو چکا تھا اس لئے اصل مالک تو حضور تھے۔ خیبر کے یہود گویا کہ کرایہ دار تھے۔ پھر بھی ان سے قسامت لی گئی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کرایہ دار یا خرید نے والوں سے بھی قسامت لی جاسکتی ہے۔ ن سکان : ساکن کی جمع ہے، کرایہ دار، ملاک : مالک کی جمع ہے زمین کے اصل مالک، اهل نظته : خطہ والے، زمین والے۔
And tenants do not enter into qasamah with the owners according to Abu Hanifah. And qasamah will be upon the people of the land (ahl al-khattah), not upon the buyers, even if only one of them remains. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, those who are the original owners of the land, i.e., those to whom the ruler assigned the land at the time of conquest by writing and handing over, from those people qasamah will be taken. Those who have taken houses on rent or live on purchased land, qasamah will not be taken from them, even if the original owner is alone, only from him will qasamah be taken. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the tenant or later purchaser of land and the original owner—from all of them qasamah will be taken. Because they could be partners in the killing, or they could have information about the killers. Therefore, from all residents of the neighborhood, oaths will be taken. (2) Oaths were taken from the Jews of Khaybar, and no distinction was made between original owners and tenants; rather, oaths were taken from all. Moreover, at that time those people were not the original owners. Because Khaybar had been conquered, so the original owner was the Prophet. The Jews of Khaybar were effectively tenants. Yet qasamah was taken from them, indicating that qasamah can be taken from tenants or purchasers as well. 'Sukkan' is plural of 'sakin', tenant; 'mullak' is plural of 'malik', original owner of land; 'ahl al-khattah': people of the land, landowners.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school. Abu Hanifah holds that only the original landowners (ahl al-khattah), i.e., those granted land at the time of conquest, are subject to qasamah. Tenants and later buyers are not included, even if only one original owner survives. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that tenants and buyers are also included because they may be involved or have information. He supports his view by citing the practice of the Prophet with the Jews of Khaybar, who were effectively tenants but were made to swear oaths. The passage then defines key terms: 'sukkan' (tenants) and 'mullak' (original owners). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically Abu Hanifah's view in this context.

Key Terms
سکان (sukkān): Tenants or residents who are not original owners.
ملّک (mullāk): Original landowners, those granted land at the time of conquest.
اهل الخطة (ahl al-khaṭṭah): People of the land, the original inhabitants granted land by the ruler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, who is subject to qasamah when a body is found in a house?
A) The current tenant
B) The original landowner only
C) Both the owner and tenant
D) All residents of the neighborhood

Key Takeaway
In qasamah, liability is tied to permanent original ownership, not mere residence, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Qasamah on Passengers and Sailors When Slain Found on Ship
Ruling on liability when a slain body is found aboard a ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah when a slain body is found on a ship and identify the condition that triggers it.

Core Idea
Qasamah is wajib on all passengers and crew when a slain body with wounds is found on a ship.

This lesson extends the principle of qasamah to the unique context of a ship. The passage establishes that if a slain body is discovered aboard, both passengers and sailors are collectively subject to qasamah. The ruling relies on an athar from al-Thawri as proof, which ties liability to the presence of a wound on the body.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qasamah (collective oath) upon the passengers and sailors when a slain body is found on a ship. The ruling is that it is wajib upon them.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from al-Thawri narrated in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. It states that if a slain with a wound is found among a people, the blood money is upon them; if no wound, nothing unless specific evidence.
This athar is a sunnah ahad, zanni in both thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar establishes that the group in whose midst the body is found bears liability if there is a wound. This is applied analogously to the ship: the passengers and crew are the group.
The presence of a wound is a condition for qasamah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school holds this position; other schools may require more specific evidence before imposing qasamah on a group.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the ruling
When a body with wounds is found on a ship, qasamah is wajib on all passengers and crew. If no wound, no qasamah unless bayyinah exists against an individual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد القتيل في سفينة فالقسامة على من فيها من الركاب والملاحين۔ اگر مقتول کشتی میں پایا گیا تو قسامت ان پر ہے جو اس میں سوار ہیں اور ملاحوں پر۔ کشتی میں لاش پائی گئی تو ظاہری علامت یہی ہے کہ انہیں لوگوں میں سے کسی ایک نے مارا ہے اس لئے قسامت انہیں لوگوں پر ہے (۲) اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن الشورى قال اذا وجد القتيل في قوم به اثر كان عقله عليهم واذا لم يكن به اثر لم يكن على العاقلة شيء الا ان تقوم البينة على احد (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۰ نمبر ۱۸۲۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جن لوگوں کے درمیان مقتول پایا جائے انہیں لوگوں پر قسم ہوگی۔
And if the slain is found in a ship, then qasamah is upon those who are on it from the passengers and sailors. If the slain is found in a ship, then qasamah is upon those who are aboard and the sailors. When the corpse is found in the ship, the apparent sign is that one of these people killed him, so qasamah is upon these people. (2) An athar has already passed: From al-Thawri, he said: 'If the slain is found among a people and there is a wound on him, then his blood money is upon them. If there is no wound, then there is nothing upon the 'aqilah unless evidence is established against someone.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 40, no. 18282). From this athar, it is understood that among whichever people the slain is found, the oath is upon those people.

Commentary
This ruling extends the principle to a ship. If a slain body is found on a ship, qasamah is imposed on the passengers and crew (sailors). The reasoning is the same: the location of the body provides apparent evidence that someone among them is the killer. The author references a previous athar from al-Thawri which states that if a body with a wound is found among a group, the blood money is upon them; if no wound, then no liability unless specific evidence exists. This athar supports the general principle that the group in whose midst the body is found bears responsibility.

Key Terms
ملاحین (mallāḥīn): Sailors or crew members of a ship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the owner of the ship
C) The passengers and sailors

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is wajib on the entire group (passengers and crew) among which a slain body with wounds is found on a ship.

Qasamah on Neighborhood Mosque
Ruling statement on qasamah location

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that qasamah is wajib on the residents of a neighborhood when a slain body is found in their local mosque, and distinguish this case from other locations.

Core Idea
Finding a slain body in a neighborhood mosque makes qasamah wajib on its people — the mosque’s local affiliation determines liability.

Qasamah is a procedure of collective oaths in cases of suspected murder when there is no direct evidence. The place where the body is found plays a crucial role in determining who must perform the oaths. This lesson focuses on a specific scenario: a body discovered in a mosque belonging to a particular neighborhood. The ruling is clear and straightforward, based on the apparent evidence that the locals are the likely perpetrators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location and its significance
Note that the body is found in a masjid mahallah (neighborhood mosque), not a central congregational mosque. The mosque's association with the neighborhood is the key factor.
The Arabic term 'مسجد محلة' specifically ties the mosque to the residents.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that qasamah is wajib (obligatory) upon the people of that neighborhood.
The source uses 'فالقسامة على أهلها' — 'then qasamah is upon its people.'
3
Understand the reasoning
The apparent evidence (zahir) indicates that the neighborhood residents killed the person and placed the body in their own mosque. This presumption is the basis for imposing qasamah.
The text says 'ظاهر هو أن هذا المحلة والوں نے قتل کر کے مسجد میں ڈال دیا ہے' (it is apparent that the people of that neighborhood killed and placed him).
4
Distinguish from other mosques
This ruling applies only to a neighborhood-specific mosque, not to the main congregational mosque (jami') or a market mosque. Those cases would have different rules.
The common misunderstanding is to generalize to all mosques; the source limits it to masjid mahallah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد في مسجد محلة فالقسامة على اهلها۔ اگر پایا جائے محلے کی مسجد میں میت تو قسامت اہل محلہ پر ہے۔ محلہ کی مسجد میں مقتول پایا گیا تو ظاہر ہی ہے کہ اس محلے والوں نے قتل کر کے مسجد میں ڈال دیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس محلے والے پر قسامت واجب ہوگی۔ اثر او پر گزر گیا ہے۔
And if he is found in the mosque of a neighborhood, then qasamah is upon its people. If the deceased is found in the mosque of the neighborhood, it is apparent that the people of that neighborhood killed him and placed him in the mosque. Therefore, qasamah is obligatory upon the people of that neighborhood. The athar has passed previously.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This is a clear ruling: if a slain body is discovered in a mosque that belongs to a specific neighborhood (masjid mahallah), the residents of that neighborhood are subject to qasamah. The reasoning is that the mosque is specifically associated with that neighborhood; therefore, the apparent evidence points to them as the killers. The author references a previous athar to support this principle. This ruling applies only to a neighborhood mosque, not the main congregational mosque (jami').

Key Terms
مسجد محلة (masjid maḥallah): A mosque specific to a particular neighborhood, as opposed to a central congregational mosque.
قسامة (qasamah): A procedure of fifty oaths taken by the defendants in a murder case where there is no direct evidence; if they refuse, they are liable for blood money.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is wajib on residents of a neighborhood when a murdered body is found in their local mosque due to apparent evidence.

No Qasamah for Slain in Congregational Mosque or Public Street
Ruling on liability when a slain body is found in a public place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a slain body is found in a public place and explain why qasamah is not imposed.

Core Idea
No qasamah for a body found in a public place; the public treasury pays the blood money.

The final ruling of this chapter addresses a situation where a slain body is discovered not in a confined neighbourhood but in a space shared by the entire city—the congregational mosque or a main public street. Because no specific group can be connected to the scene, the usual procedure of qasamah (collective oath) does not apply. However, Islamic law ensures the victim's blood is not wasted by placing the financial responsibility on the public treasury (bayt al-māl).

Guided Path
1
Identify the locations covered
Note that the ruling applies specifically to two types of public spaces: the jāmiʿ mosque (the central congregational mosque) and the public street (al-shāriʿ al-ʿāmm). Both belong to the entire city, not to any single neighbourhood or group.
2
State the negative ruling on qasamah
The passage states clearly: 'there is no qasamah in it.' Qasamah—the collective oath and liability—is not required here because there is no specific local community to hold accountable.
Qasamah is used when a body is found in a particular locality and the killer is unknown.
3
Determine the source of diyah
Since no one is individually or collectively at fault, the blood money (diyah) is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-māl). This ensures the victim's life is compensated even when the killer cannot be identified.
The treasury bears the cost to prevent the victim's blood from being shed in vain (lā yabṭulu damuhu).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد في الجامع والشارع سے قسامت لی جائے گی۔ اگر پایا جائے جامع مسجد میں یا شارع عام پر تو اس میں قسامت نہیں ہے اور دیت بیت المال پر ہے۔ جامع مسجد پورے شہر والوں کی ہے، اسی طرح عام سڑک پورے شہر والوں کے لئے ہے، معلوم نہیں کس نے مار ڈالا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی ایک محلہ والا اس کا مجرم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کسی پر قسامت لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور اس کا خون باطل نہ ہو اس لئے بیت المال پر اس کی دیت ہوگی۔
And if he is found in the congregational mosque and public street, qasamah will be taken? Actually it says: And if he is found in the congregational mosque or public street, then there is no qasamah in it, and the blood money is upon the public treasury. The congregational mosque belongs to the entire city, similarly the public street is for the entire city; it is not known who killed him. Therefore, no single neighborhood person is the criminal. Hence, qasamah is not obligatory upon anyone. And so that his blood is not in vain, his blood money is upon the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This final ruling addresses bodies found in public spaces that do not belong to any particular group. The congregational mosque (al-jami') and the main public street (al-shari' al-'amm) are for the entire city; therefore, no specific neighborhood can be blamed. Since there is no apparent evidence, qasamah is not imposed on anyone. However, to ensure the victim's blood is not wasted, the diyah is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). This reflects the principle that if liability cannot be assigned to a specific group, the state bears the financial responsibility.

Key Terms
بیت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Muslim state, used for public expenses and, in this case, diyah for unrecognized homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slain body is found in the main congregational mosque of a city, what is the ruling?
A) Qasamah is on all residents of the city
B) Qasamah on the neighborhood of the mosque
C) No qasamah; diyah from the public treasury
D) No diyah at all because the place is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
When a slain body is found in a truly public space (congregational mosque or main street), qasamah is waived and the public treasury pays the blood money.

General Principle of Qasamah on Residents
States the general rule for qasamah and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that qasamah is wajib upon original owners (ahl al-khittah) only and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with Imam Abu Yusuf who extends it to all residents.

Core Idea
Qasamah is wajib upon original owners of a district, not upon tenants or buyers, but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

This lesson opens the chapter on qasamah (oaths in unresolved homicides) with a general rule and an important intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that only the original residents of a locality bear the qasamah, not later settlers. However, Imam Abu Yusuf argues that all residents—owners, tenants, and buyers—should be equally liable. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying qasamah in communities with mixed tenure.

Guided Path
1
State the matn ruling
Identify the act (qasamah) and the ruling from the matn: it is upon ahl al-khittah (original district residents) only, not upon buyers (al-mushtarin).
The matn is the base rule of the school.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf (the companion of Abu Hanifa) disagrees: he includes tenants and buyers as subjects of qasamah.
This is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the opposing dalil
Examine the evidence cited for Abu Yusuf's view: the Khaybar incident where the Prophet took qasamah from all Jewish residents, even though they were tenants (after conquest).
This hadith suggests that residence, not ownership, is the criterion.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under the matn, only the original owner must swear; under Abu Yusuf, all residents must swear.
The difference affects the number of oaths and the burden on the community.
5
Note the tarjih
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is the matn view (Abu Hanifa), though the commentator seems sympathetic to Abu Yusuf.
Later Hanafi jurists generally adopt the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث)
۳۵۳
باب القسامة
تعالى وهى على اهل الخطة دون المشترين ولو بقى منهم واحد
(ويليه شرح) جو لوگ کرایہ پر گھر لئے ہیں یا زمین کو خرید کر رہتے ہیں ان لوگوں سے قسامت نہیں لی جائے گی چاہے اصل مالک ایک ہی ہو اسی سے قسامت لی جائے گی۔
نانی امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کرایہ دار یا بعد میں زمین خرید کر رہنے والے اور اصل مالک سب سے قسامت لی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ بھی قتل میں شریک ہو سکتے ہیں۔ یا سب کو قتل کرنے والوں کی معلومات ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس لئے محلے میں رہنے والے سبھی سے قسم لی جائے گی (۲) اہل خیبر کے یہودیوں سے قسم لی تو ان میں اصل مالک اور کرایہ دار کا فرق نہیں کیا بلکہ سب سے قسم لی۔ یوں بھی اس وقت وہ لوگ اصل مالک نہیں تھے۔ کیونکہ خیبر فتح ہو چکا تھا اس لئے اصل مالک تو حضور تھے۔ خیبر کے یہود گویا کہ کرایہ دار تھے۔ پھر بھی ان سے قسامت لی گئی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کرایہ دار یا خرید نے والوں سے بھی قسامت لی جاسکتی ہے۔ ن سکان : ساکن کی جمع ہے، کرایہ دار، ملاک : مالک کی جمع ہے زمین کے اصل مالک، اہل نظته : خطہ والے، زمین والے۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 3, 353. Chapter of Qasamah. Almighty (?) And it (qasamah) is upon the people of the district, not upon the buyers, even if only one of them remains. Commentary: Those people who have rented a house or purchased land and live there, qasamah will not be taken from them; even if the original owner is one, qasamah will be taken from him. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, qasamah will be taken from the tenant or the one who later purchased the land and the original owner all together, because they could all be partners in the murder, or they could have knowledge of the murderers. Therefore, all residents of the neighborhood should take an oath. (2) Oaths were taken from the Jews of Khaybar without distinguishing between original owners and tenants; rather, oaths were taken from all. Although at that time they were not the original owners because Khaybar had been conquered, so the original owner was the Prophet. The Jews of Khaybar were effectively tenants, yet qasamah was taken from them, showing that qasamah can be taken from tenants or purchasers. Vocabulary: سکان: plural of ساکن, tenant; ملاک: plural of مالک, original land owner; اهل خطه: people of the district, land owners.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on qasamah (oaths in homicide cases) with a general rule and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that qasamah is imposed upon the original residents (ahl al-khittah) of a locality, not upon newcomers who are buyers or renters, even if only one original resident remains. The sharh explains that those who rent houses or purchase land and reside there are exempt; qasamah is only upon the original owner. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that all residents—tenants, buyers, and original owners—are equally subject to qasamah because they could all be involved in the murder or have information. To support this, the commentator refers to the incident of Khaybar where the Prophet took the oath from all Jews regardless of their status as tenants (since ownership had transferred to the Muslims). The hadith indicates that qasamah can be applied to all residents. Thus, the passage presents the two views: Imam Abu Hanifa's (narrated here) restricts qasamah to original owners, while Imam Abu Yusuf includes all residents. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not specified in this passage, but generally the Hanafi school follows the view of Imam Abu Hanifa unless otherwise stated.

Key Terms
الخِطَّة (al-khittah): A district or quarter of a city with original inhabitants (as opposed to later settlers).
السُّكَّان (sukkān): Plural of saakin; tenants or renters who live in but do not own the property.
المُشْتَرُونَ (al-mushtarīn): Buyers who have purchased land or houses in the district.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All residents including tenants and buyers
B) Only the original owners (ahl al-khittah)
C) Only the tenants
D) The entire town

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is wajib upon original owners (ahl al-khittah) only, not upon tenants or buyers, per the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school.

Qasamah for a Body Found in a Ship
Ruling with proof from precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah when a body is found on a ship and explain the proof from the precedent of al-Shurayh.

Core Idea
Discovery of a body on a ship creates a presumption that someone among the passengers or crew is the murderer, making qasamah wajib on them.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in the law of qasamah: when a murdered body is found on a ship. The matn rules that qasamah (oaths) must be taken by every passenger and crew member. The sharh explains the reasoning—the location of the body itself serves as an indication ('athar') of involvement—and supports it with a precedent from the great judge al-Shurayh. You will learn the ruling, its basis, and how the Hanafi school analogizes from a general principle to a specific context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being judged? The act is: a murdered body is found on a ship. The ruling: qasamah is wajib upon all those present in the ship—both passengers (al-rukkaab) and crew (al-mallaahoon).
Qasamah is a collective oath of innocence required from the inhabitants of a locality when a dead body is found.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the sharh provide? It cites an athar (precedent) from al-Shurayh: when a murdered person is found among a people and there is a visible mark of injury (athar) on the body, the blood money is upon them. If no mark, then the 'aqila is not liable unless specific evidence exists.
The athar is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. It is a mursal tradition (from a tabi'i directly, not a Companion).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the athar apply to the ship case? The 'athar' (mark) is analogized to the mere presence of the body on the ship. Just as a wound mark indicates the people present may have caused it, the presence of the body in the ship indicates that someone on board is responsible.
This is a form of qiyas (analogy): the ship is like the locality (qawm), and the body's location is like the mark.
4
Understand the scope of liability
Who exactly is liable? The matn explicitly includes both passengers (ركاب) and sailors (ملاحون). The margin note from Imam al-Thawri reinforces that the 'aqila (here the people on the ship) bear the blood money if a mark is found.
This ruling is specific to ships; for land, similar qasamah rules apply to the inhabitants of the locality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۲۰] (۱۴) وان وجد القتيل في سفينة فالقسامة على من فيها من الركاب والملاحين
(ويليه شرح) اگر مقتول کشتی میں پایا گیا تو قسامت ان پر ہے جو اس میں سوار ہیں اور ملاحوں پر۔ کشتی میں لاش پائی گئی تو ظاہری علامت یہی ہے کہ انہیں لوگوں میں سے کسی ایک نے مارا ہے اس لئے قسامت انہیں لوگوں پر ہے (۲) اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن الشورى قال اذا وجد القتيل في قوم به اثر كان عقله عليهم واذا لم يكن به اثر لم يكن على العاقلة شيء الا ان تقوم البينة على احد (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۴۰ نمبر ۱۸۲۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جن لوگوں کے درمیان مقتول پایا جائے انہیں لوگوں پر قسم ہوگی۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضرت ثوری فرماتے ہیں کہ کوئی مقتول کسی قوم میں پایا گیا ہو اور اس پر زخم کا اثر ہو تو اس کی دیت ان پر ہوگی اور اگر اثر نہ ہوتو عاقلہ پر کچھ نہیں ہوگی مگر یہ کہ کسی ایک پر قتل کا بعینہ قائم کر دے۔
(14) And if the murdered person is found in a ship, then the qasamah is upon those who are in it, both passengers and sailors. Commentary: If a body is found in a ship, the apparent sign is that someone among these people killed him, so qasamah is upon these people. (2) A precedent has passed: from al-Shurayh: he said: When a murdered person is found among a people and there is a mark on him, his blood money is upon them; and if there is no mark, there is nothing upon the 'āqila except if evidence establishes it against someone. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 40, no. 18282) From this precedent it is understood that the people among whom the murdered person is found, the oath is upon them. Margin note (a): Imam al-Thawri says: If a murdered person is found among a people and there is a mark of injury on him, his blood money is upon them; and if there is no mark, there is nothing upon the 'āqila unless someone is positively identified as the murderer.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for when a murdered body is discovered on a ship. The matn states that qasamah is required from all passengers and sailors on board. The sharh explains the rationale: the presence of the body on the ship creates a strong presumption that the murder was committed by someone among those on the ship, so they must take oaths to clear themselves. The commentator then supports this with an athar (precedent) from al-Shurayh, a famous judge, who states that when a body is found among a people with a visible mark of injury, the blood money is upon them; if no mark, then the 'āqila (responsible clan) is not liable unless specific evidence is produced. This athar is used to analogize that the presence of the body itself is a kind of 'mark' indicating involvement. The margin note from Imam al-Thawri reinforces the same principle: if there is a wound mark, they are liable; if no mark, they are not unless proven otherwise. Here, the mark is replaced by the fact that the body is in the ship, so qasamah applies. The ruling is clear: qasamah is wajib upon all persons on the ship.

Key Terms
الرِّكابُ (al-rukkaab): Passengers on the ship.
المَلَّاحُونَ (al-mallaahoon): Sailors or crew of the ship.
الأَثَرُ (al-athar): A visible mark or indication of injury on the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the ship's owner
B) Only the passengers
C) Both passengers and sailors
D) The nearest port authority

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is wajib on all occupants of a ship when a body is found aboard, per the precedent of al-Shurayh.

Qasamah for a Body in a Neighborhood Mosque
Ruling on qasamah for a body found in a neighborhood mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that qasamah is wajib upon the residents when a body is found in a neighborhood mosque and explain the reasoning based on circumstantial evidence.

Core Idea
Location determines liability: a body in a neighborhood mosque puts qasamah on its residents.

This brief ruling from the matn addresses a specific scenario: a murdered body is discovered in a mosque that belongs to a particular neighborhood. The text declares that the residents of that neighborhood must perform qasamah (a collective oath of innocence). The commentary clarifies that the location itself creates a strong presumption of local involvement, making the oath obligatory. Understanding this rule requires grasping how the Hanafi school uses spatial association as evidence of potential culpability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location
Note that the mosque is specified as 'masjid mahallah' – a neighborhood mosque, not the central city mosque (al-jami'). This distinction is crucial because the ruling hinges on the mosque being associated with a specific group of residents.
2
Determine the legal effect
The ruling states that qasamah is 'upon its people' (ala ahliha). This means the residents of that neighborhood must take oaths to clear themselves of involvement. It is wajib (obligatory) upon them collectively.
Qasamah is a pre-Islamic practice retained in Hanafi law for cases of unsolved homicide with strong circumstantial evidence.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The commentary explains the logic: finding the body in the neighborhood mosque strongly indicates that the murder was committed by someone from that locality. They would have easiest access and motive to dispose of the body there. Thus, the location creates a presumption of guilt that must be rebutted by oath.
This reasoning is based on the athar (precedent) of Shurayh, which the commentator references.
4
Apply to similar scenarios
Consider how this rule would apply if the body were found in a mosque used by multiple neighborhoods (al-jami'). The Hanafi ruling would differ—qasamah would then be on the residents of the area surrounding the mosque, not the entire city. The key is the degree of association between the location and a defined community.
This extension is not in the text but follows from the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۳۲۱) (۱۵) وان وجد في مسجد محلة فالقسامة على اهلها
(ويليه شرح) اگر محلے کی مسجد میں میت پائی جائے تو قسامت اہل محلہ پر ہے۔ محلہ کی مسجد میں مقتول پایا گیا تو ظاہر ہی ہے کہ اس محلے والوں نے قتل کر کے مسجد میں ڈال دیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس محلے والے پر قسامت واجب ہوگی۔ اثر او پر گزر گیا ہے۔
(15) And if he is found in the mosque of a neighborhood, then the qasamah is upon its people. Commentary: If a body is found in the mosque of a neighborhood, qasamah is upon the people of that neighborhood. The body found in the neighborhood mosque indicates clearly that the people of that neighborhood killed him and placed him there. Therefore, qasamah is obligatory upon the people of that neighborhood. The precedent mentioned earlier has passed.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This brief ruling addresses a body found in a local mosque. The matn states that qasamah falls on the people of that neighborhood (ahl al-mahallah). The sharh explains the reasoning: the presence of the body in the neighborhood mosque strongly suggests that the murder was committed by someone in that neighborhood, as they would be the ones most likely to have access. Therefore, they must swear oaths to disprove involvement. The commentator references an earlier precedent (the same athar from al-Shurayh) to support the principle that the location implies responsibility. No other proofs are given here; it is a straightforward application of the rule that the locale determines liability.

Key Terms
مَسْجِدُ مَحَلَّة (masjid mahallah): A mosque belonging to a specific neighborhood or quarter of a town.
أَهْلُهَا (ahluha): The residents of that neighborhood.

Qasamah for Body Found in Public Space: No Qasamah, Diyah from Treasury
Ruling on qasamah for body in public space with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a body is found in a central mosque or public street, explain why qasamah is not applied, and identify the basis for diyah from the public treasury.

Core Idea
Public space = no single group liable; treasury pays to prevent wasted blood.

In earlier lessons, we saw that qasamah (oaths) applies when a body is found in a private area belonging to a specific group. But what if the body is discovered in a truly public space like the central mosque or main road? This lesson presents the Hanafi position: no qasamah, and the blood money is paid from the state treasury. We will work through the matn, the commentary's reasoning, and the proofs that establish this important principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location and its legal significance
The matn specifies two locations: al-jami' (central mosque) and al-shari' al-a'zam (main street). These are public spaces belonging to the entire community, not to any single neighborhood. This is the key difference from previous cases where the body was found in a specific alley or house.
The commentary emphasizes that these places belong to the whole city, so no one group can be singled out.
2
State the ruling and the reason
The ruling is: 'la qasamata fihi' (no qasamah) and 'al-diyatu 'ala bayt al-mal' (blood money on the public treasury). The reason: since the killer is unknown and the location is public, suspecting a specific group would be unjust. Qasamah is therefore not imposed.
Note the Islamic principle that blood should not be wasted; compensation must be provided.
3
Analyze the proofs cited in the sharh
The commentary provides three proofs: (a) a saying of Ali that a body found in a desert gets diyah from treasury; (b) the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl where the Prophet paid from charity camels; (c) an incident in Kufa where Ali paid from treasury for a death in the central mosque. Each proof shows that when no specific person is liable, the state bears the cost.
These proofs extend the ruling beyond mosque/street to any unowned public place (e.g., desert).
4
Understand the operative principle
The overarching principle is that the life of a Muslim is inviolable, and if the killer cannot be identified, the state must not let the blood go unavenged. The public treasury ensures compensation, preserving the dignity of the victim.
This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on avoiding wasted blood (dam la yudraku).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۲۲] (۱۶) وان وجد في الجامع والشارع الاعظم فلا قسامة فيه والدية على بيت المال
(ويليه شرح) اگر پایا جائے جامع مسجد میں یا شارع عام پر تو اس میں قساوت نہیں ہے اور دیت بیت المال پر ہے۔ جامع مسجد پورے شہر والوں کی ہے، اسی طرح عام سڑک پورے شہر والوں کے لئے ہے، معلوم نہیں کس نے مار ڈالا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی ایک محلہ والا اس کا مجرم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کسی پر قسامت لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور اس کا خون باطل نہ ہو اس لئے بیت المال پر اس کی دیت ہوگی
(وتتمة)  وقال على ايما قتيل وجد بفلاة من الارض فديته من بيت المال لكيلا يبطل دم في الاسلام (الف) (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۳۶ نمبر ۱۸۲۶۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت ایسی جگہ پائی جائے جہاں کسی ایک محلے پر شبہ نہ ہو سکے تو قسامت نہیں ہوگی اور اس کی دیت بیت المال پر ہوگی (۳) حضور نے عبداللہ بن سہل بن زید کی دیت خود اپنی جانب سے سو اونٹ ادا کی تھی فكره رسول الله الله ان يطل دمه فوداه مائة من ابل الصدقة (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب القسامة ص ۱۰۱۸ نمبر ۶۸۹۸ مسلم شریف ، کتاب القسامة ص ۵۴ نمبر ۱۶۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں قیامت نہ ہو وہاں دیت بیت المال پر ہوگی (۴) مسلم بن يزيد بن مذكور ان الناس از دحموا في المسجد الجامع بالكوفة يوم الجمعة فافرجوا عن قتيل فوداه علی بن ابی طالب من بيت المال (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۷۵ الرجل يقتل في الزحام ج خامس ، ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۲۷۸۴۷)
حاشیه : (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا کوئی مقتول جنگل میں پایا جائے تو اس کی دیت بیت المال سے دی جائے گی تا کہ اسلام میں خون بیکار نہ جائے
(ب) حضور نے ناپسند کیا کہ مقتول کا خون بیکار جائے اس لئے صدقہ کے اونٹ سے سو اونٹ دیت ادا کی
(ج) یزید بن مذکور فرماتے ہیں کہ لوگوں نے جمعہ کے دن کوفہ کی جامع مسجد میں بھیڑ کی۔ جس کی وجہ سے ایک آدمی مر گیا تو حضرت علی نے بیت المال سے اس کی دیت دی
(16) And if he is found in the central mosque or the main street, there is no qasamah therein, and the blood money is upon the public treasury. Commentary: If the body is found in the central mosque or a public street, there is no qasamah and the blood money is on the public treasury. The central mosque belongs to the entire city, as does the public road; it is not known who killed him. So no single neighborhood can be considered culpable, so qasamah is not obligatory on anyone. And so that his blood not be wasted, his blood money is upon the public treasury. (Continuation) And he said: Any murdered person found in a desert, his blood money is from the public treasury so that no blood is wasted in Islam. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 36, no. 18269) From this precedent it is understood that if a body is found in a place where no particular neighborhood can be suspected, there is no qasamah and his blood money is on the public treasury. (3) The Prophet paid the blood money of Abdullah ibn Sahl ibn Zaid himself with one hundred camels from the charity camels because he disliked that his blood should be wasted. (b) (Bukhari, Bab al-Qasamah, p. 1018, no. 6898; Muslim, Kitab al-Qasamah, p. 54, no. 1669) From this hadith it is understood that wherever there is no qasamah, the blood money is on the public treasury. (4) Muslim ibn Yazid ibn Mazkoor: The people crowded in the central mosque of Kufa on Friday, and they cleared away a dead body, and Ali ibn Abi Talib paid his blood money from the public treasury. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 5, p. 445, no. 27847) Margin notes: (a) Ali said: If any murdered person is found in a desert, his blood money should be given from the public treasury so that no blood is wasted in Islam. (b) The Prophet disliked that the blood of the murdered person be wasted, so he paid the blood money of one hundred camels from the charity camels. (c) Yazid ibn Mazkoor said: People crowded in the central mosque of Kufa on Friday, causing a man to die, and Ali paid his blood money from the public treasury.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where a body is found in a central mosque (al-jamiʿ) or a main public street. The key difference from the previous cases is that these are public spaces belonging to the entire city, not to a single neighborhood. Therefore, no specific group can be held responsible, and qasamah (oaths) cannot be imposed on anyone. To ensure that the victim's blood is not left unavenged or uncompensated, the blood money (diyah) is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). The sharh provides multiple proofs: (a) an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib stating that for a body found in a desert, diyah comes from the treasury; (b) the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl where the Prophet paid from the charity camels; and (c) an incident from Kufa where Ali paid from the treasury for a death in a crowd in the central mosque. These establish the principle that in places belonging to the general public, the state bears the financial responsibility. The margin notes reinforce the same idea. Note: The matn is about central mosque and main street; the proofs also mention desert, but the ruling is extended to any place that does not point to a specific group.

Key Terms
الجامِعُ (al-jaamiʿ): The central congregational mosque of a city.
الشارِعُ الأَعْظَمُ (al-shaariʿ al-aʿzam): The main public road or street.
بَيْتُ المالِ (bayt al-maal): The public treasury of the Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a body is found in the central mosque or main street, what happens?
A) Qasamah is taken from all neighborhoods
B) No qasamah, and blood money is from the public treasury
C) The person who discovered the body must pay
D) The killer is presumed to be from the nearest house

Key Takeaway
When a body is found in a public space that does not belong to any specific group, the Hanafi school imposes diyah on the public treasury to avoid wasted blood, and no qasamah applies.

Qasamah for a Body Found in an Uninhabited Wilderness
Ruling on qasamah and diyah for a body found in a wilderness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a body is found in an uninhabited wilderness and explain why the blood money is paid from the public treasury.

Core Idea
A body found in a wilderness triggers no qasamah, but the state ensures compensation from the treasury to prevent wasted blood.

When a body is discovered in a remote wilderness far from any settlement, there is no specific community that can be held responsible. The Hanafi school rules that qasamah does not apply in such a case. However, the victim's life is not worthless; the Islamic state guarantees blood money from the public treasury to honor the sanctity of Muslim blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation: a body is found in an uninhabited wilderness (بريَّة) with no buildings or settlements nearby.
The opposite case is when the body is found between two villages, where the nearer village bears responsibility.
2
Understand the term 'هدر'
The matn says 'فهو هدر' meaning 'it is wasted'. However, the sharh clarifies that this applies only to qasamah, not to compensation. The blood money is still due.
A common misunderstanding is that no payment is made at all.
3
Note the exemption from qasamah
Qasamah is not required because there is no specific neighborhood on which to impose it. The absence of habitation removes the basis for qasamah.
The proof for this is the athar from Ali.
4
Examine the proof (athar)
The athar states: 'Any murdered person found in a desert, his blood money is from the public treasury so that no blood is wasted in Islam.' This establishes the duty of the treasury.
The athar is considered a mursal hadith with zanni thubut but clear dalala.
5
State the mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling is: No qasamah, but the blood money (diyah) is wajib upon the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
This ruling is agreed upon within the Hanafi school and is practiced accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۴۲۳ ) وان وجد في بريَّة ليس بقربها عمارة فهو هدر [ ۲۴۲۴] (۱۸) وان وجد بين قريتين كان على اقربهما.
(ويليه شرح) اگر پایا گیا جنگل میں جس کے قریب آبادی نہ ہو تو اس کا خون بیکار ہے۔ یہاں بھی قریب میں کوئی محلہ نہیں ہے جس پر قسامت واجب کریں۔ اس لئے قیامت نہیں ہوگی اور دیت بیت المال سے دی جائے گی۔ اس کے لئے اثر پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔
(وتتمة) وقال على ايما قتيل وجد بفلاة من الارض فديته من بيت المال لكيلا يبطل دم في الاسلام (الف) (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب القسامة ج عاشر ص ۳۶ نمبر ۱۸۲۶۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت ایسی جگہ پائی جائے جہاں کسی ایک محلے پر شبہ نہ ہو سکے تو قسامت نہیں ہوگی اور اس کی دیت بیت المال پر ہوگی
(17) And if he is found in a wilderness with no habitation near it, then it is wasted (a lost case). (18) And if found between two villages, it is upon the nearer one. Commentary: If found in a forest with no settlement nearby, his blood is wasted. Here too, there is no nearby neighborhood on which to impose qasamah, so there is no qasamah, and the blood money is paid from the public treasury. A precedent has passed for this. (Continuation) And he said: Any murdered person found in a desert, his blood money is from the public treasury so that no blood is wasted in Islam. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 36, no. 18269) From this precedent it is understood that if a body is found in a place where no single neighborhood can be suspected, there is no qasamah and his blood money is on the public treasury.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a body found in an uninhabited wilderness. The matn uses the term 'هدر' meaning wasted or unavenged. However, the sharh clarifies that this does not mean no compensation; rather, since no specific neighborhood can be held responsible, qasamah is not applicable, but the diyah (blood money) must still be paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) to prevent the blood from being wasted. The commentator references the same athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib that was mentioned in the previous lesson, which states that any body found in a desert should have its diyah from the treasury. Thus, even in a wilderness, the state ensures compensation. The ruling effectively equates to that of the central mosque and public street.

Key Terms
بَرِيَّة (bariyyah): A wilderness or desert with no habitation.
هَدْر (hadr): Literally wasted; here it means the blood is not subject to qasamah but not necessarily unpaid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a body is found in an uninhabited wilderness, what is the ruling according to the matn?
A) The blood is wasted and no one pays
B) The nearest town pays the blood money
C) The blood is wasted (no qasamah) but blood money is from the public treasury
D) The finder of the body must pay

Key Takeaway
When a body is found in an uninhabited wilderness, qasamah is not applicable, but the public treasury pays the blood money to prevent the blood from being wasted.
