Ruling on Robbers Caught Before Taking Property or Killing
States ruling and proof for imprisoning highway robbers caught before crime

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for highway robbers caught before completing the crime and explain the evidence from Quran 5:33 and the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz.

Core Idea
Incomplete highway robbery is punished by imprisonment until repentance, not fixed hadd.

In the Hanafi school, the severity of punishment for highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) is graded according to the completion of the crime. This lesson examines a specific scenario: robbers caught before they take any property or kill anyone. The ruling is that they are to be imprisoned until they show repentance. We will explore the textual evidence from the Quran and the practice of the early Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz that supports this graduated approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act described? (Robbers caught before taking property or killing). What is the ruling? (Imprisonment until repentance).
The ruling is explicitly stated in the first line of the passage.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage provides two evidences: the Quranic verse (5:33) on muharaba and the effect (athar) from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz concerning a thief. Identify both.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the fourth punishment in the verse, 'banishment from the land' (nafy), apply to this case? The Hanafi school interprets nafy as imprisonment.
This is the key interpretive move: nafy = imprisonment, not mere exile.
4
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
Other schools may interpret nafy differently (e.g., literal exile). The Hanafi view is specific and defended by the context of the verse and the need for a practical, rehabilitative punishment.
The passage indicates this is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأخذوا قبل ان ياخذوا مالا ولاقتلوا نفسا حبسهم الامام حتى يُحدثوا توبة [۲۵۶۲] (۴۰) وان اخذوا مال مسلم او ذمى والماخوذ اذا قسم على جماعتهم کرلے اور حرکات وسکنات سے محسوس ہو کہ اس نے ڈاکہ زنی سے توبہ کر لی ہے۔ ہاتھ پاؤں تو اس لئے نہیں کاٹے گا کہ ابھی مال نہیں لیا ہے اور قتل اس لئے نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ ابھی کسی کا خون نہیں بہایا ہے۔ ممکن ہے کہ اس کام سے پہلے وہ تو بہ کر لیتا (۲) اس اثر میں ہے۔ ان عمر بن عبد العزيز كتب في سارق لا يقطع حتى يخرج بالمتاع من الدار لعله يعرض توبة قبل ان يخرج من الدار (الف) ( مصنف ابن ابی هیة فی السارق یو خذ قبل ان يخرج من البيت بالمتاع ج خامس ص ۴۷۴ نمبر ۲۸۱۱۴ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب السارق يوجد فى البيت ولم يخرج ج عاشر ص ۱۹۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۰۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال چرا کر قبضہ کرے گا تب ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ اس ڈاکہ زن نے ابھی مال لوٹا نہیں ہے اس لئے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا صرف قید کیا جائے گا (۲) آیت محاربہ میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ انما جزء والذين يحاربون الله ورسوله ويسعون في الارض فسادا ان يقتلوا او يصلبوا او تقطع ايديهم وأرجلهم من خلاف او ينفوو من الارض ذلك لهم خزى في الدنيا ولهم في الآخرة عذاب عظیم (ب) ( آیت ۳۳ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں چار قسم کی سزا بیان کی گئی ہیں کیونکہ چار قسم کی شرارتیں ہوتی ہیں۔ ان میں سے آخری سزا یہ ہے کہ ینفوا من الارض شہر سے باہر کر دیا جائے یعنی قید کر دیا جائے۔ یہ سزا اس وقت ہے جب نہ چوری کی ہو اور نہ قتل کر سکا ہو۔ ممتنع : روکنے والا یعنی راستہ روک کر ڈاکہ زنی کرنے والا۔ قطع الطریق : راستہ کاٹنا یعنی لوگوں کو راستے میں لوٹ لینا، ڈاکہ زنی کرنا، جسم : ان کو قید کر دے۔
If they are caught before they take any property or kill anyone, the Imam imprisons them until they show repentance. [2562] (40) And if they took the property of a Muslim or a dhimmi, and the property when divided among their group... and from their movements and actions it is sensed that he has repented from highway robbery. So the hand and foot will not be cut because he has not yet taken property, and he will not be killed because he has not yet shed anyone's blood. It is possible that before this act he may repent. (2) There is an effect in this: 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz wrote regarding a thief: his hand is not cut until he takes the goods out of the house; perhaps he will turn in repentance before he leaves the house. (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, on the thief who is caught before he leaves the house with the goods, vol. 5 p. 474 no. 28114; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the thief found in the house and has not left, vol. 10 p. 196 no. 18809). From this effect it is learned that he will steal and take possession of property, then his hand will be cut. And since this highway robber has not yet looted any property, his hand will not be cut; he will only be imprisoned. (2) The verse on muharaba indicates this: 'The recompense of those who wage war against Allah and His Messenger and strive in the land to cause corruption is that they be killed or crucified or that their hands and feet be cut off from opposite sides or that they be banished from the land. That is for them a disgrace in this world, and they will have a great punishment in the Hereafter.' (b) (Verse 33 of Surah al-Ma'idah 5). In this verse, four types of punishment are mentioned because there are four types of mischief. Among them, the last punishment is that they be banished from the land, i.e., they are to be exiled from the city, meaning imprisoned. This punishment is when there is neither theft nor killing. mumtani': one who prevents, i.e., one who blocks the road to rob. qat' al-tariq: cutting the road, i.e., looting people on the road, highway robbery. jism: they are to be imprisoned.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding highway robbers (muharibun/qutta' al-tariq) who are apprehended before they have actually taken any property or killed anyone. The ruling is that the Imam is to imprison them until they manifest repentance. The reasoning is that since they have not yet committed the theft (taking property) or murder (killing a person), the prescribed hadd punishments (cutting of hand and foot, or execution) are not applicable. The author supports this ruling with two proofs: first, the practice of the Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, who ordered that a thief's hand not be cut until he actually removes the stolen goods from the house, giving him an opportunity to repent; similarly, the highway robber gets a chance. Second, the verse of muharaba (Quran 5:33) lists four punishments corresponding to four levels of crime. The fourth punishment is 'banishment from the land' (nafy min al-ard), which the Hanafi school interprets as imprisonment. This is the appropriate punishment when no property has been taken and no life has been taken. The passage also defines key terms: mumtani' is the one who prevents (i.e., blocks the road), and qat' al-tariq is the act of highway robbery. The commentary clarifies that the phrase 'jism' means to imprison them. Thus, the Hanafi position is that full hadd is not incurred until the crime is completed; mere preparation or attempt without completion results in a lesser discretionary punishment (ta'zir), here specified as imprisonment until repentance.

Key Terms
ممتنع (mumtani'): One who prevents or blocks; specifically a highway robber who stops people on the road to rob them.
قطع الطريق (qat' al-tariq): Cutting the road; highway robbery involving blocking the road and looting travelers.
ينفوا من الارض (yunfaw min al-ard): Banishment from the land; interpreted in this text as imprisonment (qaid) or exile, applicable when no property or life is taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What punishment does the Hanafi school prescribe for highway robbers who are caught before taking any property or killing anyone?
A) Cutting of the right hand and left foot
B) Imprisonment until they show repentance
C) Execution by the sword
D) Exile from the city with confiscation of property

Key Takeaway
Highway robbers caught before completing the crime are subject to discretionary imprisonment, not fixed hadd, based on Quran 5:33 and the precedent of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz.

Hadd for Highway Robbers: Conditions and Evidence
States ruling and proof for cutting hands and feet of robbers who took property >= 10 dirhams each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the hadd of cutting hands and feet applies to highway robbers and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Highway robbers who steal protected property worth ≥10 dirhams each face cutting of right hand and left foot.

This passage establishes the specific conditions required for applying the hadd punishment of cutting the right hand and left foot to highway robbers (muharibin). It clarifies that the punishment is not automatic but depends on the protected status of the property and the value per robber. The author supports the ruling with the Quranic verse (5:33) and the famous hadith of the tribes of 'Ukl and 'Urayna. Understanding these conditions is essential to correctly apply the shar'i punishment and avoid exceeding its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is highway robbery (muharaba) where the robbers take property. The ruling is a fixed prescribed punishment (hadd) of cutting the right hand and left foot from opposite sides.
This is distinct from the theft hadd (cutting only the right hand) because highway robbery causes greater public harm.
2
List the conditions for the hadd
Two key conditions: 1) The property must be from a Muslim or dhimmi (protected person – mahfuz). 2) Each robber's share of the loot must be at least 10 dirhams (or equivalent value). Without these, the hadd is not applied.
Property of a harbi (enemy combatant) is not protected; taking it does not trigger the hadd.
3
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The passage cites two pieces of evidence: Quran 5:33 ("cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides") and the hadith of 'Ukl and 'Urayna where the Prophet (peace be upon him) cut hands and feet of robbers who stole camels and killed shepherds.
The hadith is ahad but considered sahih and is used to demonstrate the practical application of the Quranic verse.
4
Trace the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The Quranic verse specifies cutting from opposite sides, which the Hanafi school interprets as the right hand and left foot. The hadith confirms this: the Prophet cut their hands and feet, and because the robbers also killed, he additionally gouged their eyes. The cutting alone establishes the hadd for theft in muharaba.
The combination of theft and murder leads to additional punishment, but the hadd for purely property-taking is cutting.

(2562) (40) And if they took the property of a Muslim or a dhimmi, and the property when divided among their group... [then the ruling]. If they took the property of a Muslim or dhimmi and the taken property when divided among their group, each one gets ten dirhams or more, or something worth that much, then the Imam cuts their hands and feet from opposite sides. This group looted the property of a dhimmi or a Muslim, and they looted so much that each individual of the group gets ten dirhams or more, or the looted property gives each person so much that its value is ten dirhams, then the Imam will cut the right hand and left foot of each. It will be cut because the property of a dhimmi or Muslim is protected (mahfuz). If they loot the property of a harbi (non-Muslim enemy), the hand is not cut because his property is not protected. And it will be cut only when each one gets ten dirhams; its proof has already passed that it is not cut for less than ten dirhams. And the right hand... [hashiya]... [PAGE_438] each of them got ten dirhams or more, or something worth that much, the Imam cuts their hands and feet from opposite sides. [2563] (41) And if they killed a person and did not take any property, the Imam executes them as a prescribed punishment (hadd). Then... and the left foot both will be cut. The reason is that they are not mere thieves but highway robbers. Once highway robbery occurs, the whole area fears and does not sleep for months, and insecurity spreads throughout the region. Therefore, its punishment is made severe: the hand on one side and foot on the opposite side are cut so that he cannot commit highway robbery again. (2) The punishment for looting property has passed in the verse: 'And cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides' (verse 33 of Surah al-Ma'idah 5). In this verse, it is that the hands and feet of robbers are cut. (3) There is a hadith: Some people from the tribes of 'Ukl and 'Urayna came to the Prophet (peace be upon him), embraced Islam, and stayed in Medina. They fell ill, so the Prophet ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqah and drink their milk and urine. They did so and were cured, then they apostatized, killed the shepherds, and drove away the camels. The Prophet sent people after them; they were brought back, and he cut off their hands and feet and gouged out their eyes with hot irons, and did not cauterize them until they died. (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on muharibun from the people of kufr and ridda, p. 1005 no. 6802; Sahih Muslim, chapter on ruling of muharibun and apostates, p. 57 no. 1671). In this hadith, the hands and feet of the muharibun (highway robbers) were cut because they had stolen the camels. And because they killed the shepherds, their eyes were gouged so that they would die in agony.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings: first, the hadd punishment for highway robbers who have taken property of a Muslim or dhimmi, and second, a digression to explain the condition that each robber's share must reach the nisab of theft (10 dirhams). The author reiterates the ruling from the Quranic verse (5:33) that the punishment is cutting the right hand and left foot from opposite sides. The text specifies that this punishment applies only when the property taken is from a Muslim or a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state), because such property is considered 'mahfuz' (inviolable). Property of a harbi (an enemy belligerent) is not protected, so no hadd is applied for taking it. Additionally, the cut is only executed if each robber's share from the looted property amounts to at least ten dirhams or its equivalent, as this is the minimum value for the hadd of theft. The justification for the severity is that highway robbery causes widespread fear and insecurity, so the punishment is designed to incapacitate the criminal. The author then cites the famous hadith of the 'Ukl and 'Urayna tribes, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) applied the hadd of cutting hands and feet for robbery and murder. This hadith is used as evidence for the permissibility of combining hadd punishments (cutting for theft and execution for murder) when both crimes are committed. However, the text notes that in the case of robbery without murder, the hadd is cutting of hand and foot; if they commit murder as well, the punishment may escalate to execution (as will be covered in the next lesson).

Key Terms
محارب (muharib): One who wages war against Allah and His Messenger by committing highway robbery and spreading corruption; synonymous with qati' al-tariq.
محفوظ (mahfuz): Protected; property that is legally inviolable, specifically the property of Muslims and dhimmis.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum threshold value for applying the hadd of theft; for highway robbery, each robber's share must reach 10 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the hadd of cutting hands and feet apply to a highway robber who takes property?
A) If the property belongs to any person, regardless of value
B) If the property belongs to a Muslim or dhimmi and each robber's share is at least 10 dirhams
C) If the property belongs to a harbi and is worth more than 10 dirhams total
D) If the robbery is committed at night

Key Takeaway
The hadd of cutting hands and feet for highway robbery only applies when the property is protected (Muslim or dhimmi) and each robber's share reaches the nisab of theft (10 dirhams).

Hadd Execution for Robbers Who Kill but Take No Property
States ruling and proofs for execution as hadd, with emphasis on non-waivability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for highway robbers who kill without taking property and explain why the victim's family's forgiveness does not affect the hadd penalty.

Core Idea
Hadd for muharaba is a right of Allah; even if victims' families forgive, the Imam must execute the robber.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a specific scenario in the law of hirabah (highway robbery): when the robbers murder someone but do not take any property. The author clarifies that the fixed punishment (hadd) is execution, and this penalty is not subject to the victim's family's forgiveness because it is a right of Allah (haqq Allah) aimed at protecting public order. The ruling is supported by Quranic verse 5:33 and the prophetic practice in the hadith of 'Ukl and 'Urayna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is highway robbery (muharaba) committed with murder but without taking property. The Hanafi ruling is that the Imam executes the robber as a fixed punishment (hadd).
This is different from qisas for murder, which is a private right.
2
Understand the legal category
Recognize that muharaba is a crime against public security, hence its punishment is a right of Allah (hadd) and cannot be waived by individuals.
Hadd penalties are fixed and not subject to negotiation or forgiveness.
3
Examine the proof from the Quran and Hadith
The passage cites Quran 5:33 (amputation for those who wage war) and the hadith of 'Ukl and 'Urayna, where the Prophet executed the robbers who had killed shepherds and stolen camels.
The hadith shows that even if the victims' families might have forgiven, the Prophet still carried out the punishment.
4
Analyze the implication of forgiveness
The text explicitly states that even if the victim's heirs (awliya' al-damm) forgive, the Imam does not accept their forgiveness. This is because the hadd is a public right.
Contrast with regular murder where qisas can be commuted to diyah or forgiven.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow the family's forgiveness to commute the hadd to qisas or diyah. The Hanafi school insists on execution as hadd.
This difference arises from whether the crime is seen as primarily a private wrong or a public offense.

Source Text

[۲۵۶۳] (۴۱) وان قتلوا نفسا ولم ياخذوا مالا قتلهم الامام حدا فان اور بایاں پاؤں دونوں کاٹے جائیں گے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ صرف چور نہیں ہیں بلکہ ڈاکہ زن ہیں ۔ ایک مرتبہ ڈاکہ زنی ہو جائے تو پورا علاقہ خوف سے مہینوں نہیں سوتے ہیں۔ اور پورے علاقے میں بدامنی پھیل جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی سزا سخت رکھی گئی ہے کہ ایک طرف کا ہاتھ اور دوسری طرف کا پاؤں کاٹ دیا جائے تا کہ دوبارہ ڈاکہ زنی وہ کر سکے (۲) مال لوٹنے کی سزا آیت میں گزری او تقطع ایدیهم وارجلهم من خلاف (آیت ۳۳ سورۃ المائدۃ (۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ڈاکووں کے ہاتھ اور وپاؤں دونوں کاٹے جائیں (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ قبیلہ مکل اور قبیلہ عرینہ کے کچھ لوگ حضور کے پاس آئے وہ مسلمان ہوئے اور مدینہ میں رہنے لگے۔ لیکن ان کو بیماری لگ گئی تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ جاؤ صدقہ کے اونٹ کا دودھ اور پیشاب پیو۔ وہ اس سے صحت یاب ہو گئے لیکن بعد میں مرتد ہو گئے اور اونٹ کے چرواہوں کو قتل کر دیا اور اونٹ بھی لوٹ کر لے گئے ۔ آپ نے ان کے ہاتھ اور پاؤں کو کٹوایا اور آنکھوں میں گرم سلائی پھیر دی جس سے وہ مر گئے۔ لمبی حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن انس قال قدم على النبي الا الله نفر من عكل فاسلموا فاجتووا المدينة فامرهم ان يأتوا ابل الصدقة فيشربوا من أبوالها والبانها ففعلوا فصحوا فارتدوا وقتلوا رعاتها واستاقوا الابل فبعث في آثارهم فاتي بهم فقطع ايديهم وارجلهم وسمل اعينهم ثم لم يحسمهم حتى م ، ماتوا (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب کتاب المحاربين من اهل الكفر والردة ص ۱۰۰۵ نمبر ۶۸۰۲ ر مسلم شریف ، باب حکم المحاربين والمرتدین ص ۵۷ نمبر ا ۱۶۷) اس حدیث میں محارب اور ڈاکہ زنوں کے ہاتھ اور پاؤں دونوں کاٹے ہیں کیونکہ انہوں نے اونٹ چرایا تھا۔ اور چرواہوں کو قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے آنکھوں میں سلائی پھیر دی تا کہ تڑپ تڑپ کرمر جائیں۔
[2563] (41) And if they killed a person and did not take any property, the Imam executes them as a prescribed punishment (hadd). Then... and the left foot both will be cut. The reason is that they are not mere thieves but highway robbers. Once highway robbery occurs, the whole area fears and does not sleep for months, and insecurity spreads throughout the region. Therefore, its punishment is made severe: the hand on one side and foot on the opposite side are cut so that he cannot commit highway robbery again. (2) The punishment for looting property has passed in the verse: 'And cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides' (verse 33 of Surah al-Ma'idah 5). In this verse, it is that the hands and feet of robbers are cut. (3) There is a hadith: Some people from the tribes of 'Ukl and 'Urayna came to the Prophet (peace be upon him), embraced Islam, and stayed in Medina. They fell ill, so the Prophet ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqah and drink their milk and urine. They did so and were cured, then they apostatized, killed the shepherds, and drove away the camels. The Prophet sent people after them; they were brought back, and he cut off their hands and feet and gouged out their eyes with hot irons, and did not cauterize them until they died. (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on muharibun from the people of kufr and ridda, p. 1005 no. 6802; Sahih Muslim, chapter on ruling of muharibun and apostates, p. 57 no. 1671). In this hadith, the hands and feet of the muharibun (highway robbers) were cut because they had stolen the camels. And because they killed the shepherds, their eyes were gouged so that they would die in agony.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for highway robbers who commit murder but do not take any property. The ruling is that the Imam executes them as a fixed punishment (hadd). The text further clarifies that even if the victim's family (awliya' al-damm) forgives the killer, the Imam does not accept their forgiveness and proceeds with execution. This is because the crime of highway robbery (muharaba) is considered a crime against public order and the sovereignty of Allah, not merely a private right of the victim. Therefore, the state has the right to impose the hadd penalty regardless of the victim's family's wishes. The passage also reiterates the reasoning behind the severe punishments for highway robbers: their actions cause widespread fear and insecurity, affecting the entire community. The author then references the hadith of 'Ukl and 'Urayna, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) cut off their hands and feet and also gouged their eyes (a punishment beyond the typical hadd, possibly as a discretionary ta'zir for the murder and apostasy). This hadith serves as evidence for the permissibility of combining hadd and ta'zir punishments when multiple crimes are committed.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes; here, execution for highway robbery involving murder.
أولياء الدم (awliya' al-damm): The legal guardians or heirs of a murder victim who have the right to seek qisas or forgive.
قطع الطريق (qat' al-tariq): Highway robbery; the act of blocking roads and looting travelers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of the hadd penalty for muharaba (highway robbery) committed with murder?
A) It is a private right that can be forgiven by the victim's family.
B) It is a public right that cannot be waived by individuals.
C) It is a discretionary punishment subject to the judge's opinion.
D) It is applied only if property is taken.

Key Takeaway
Highway robbers who kill without taking property must be executed as hadd, and their punishment cannot be waived by the victim's family's forgiveness.

Permissibility of Making Nabidh in Prohibited Vessels
Ruling with proof on nabidh vessels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits making nabidh in the four vessels and identify the evidence of abrogation from the hadith.

Core Idea
Vessels don't make drinks haram; only intoxication does.

This passage tackles a classic fiqh topic: the abrogation of an initial prohibition. The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade using certain vessels for nabidh to wean people away from wine. Once the community was ready, he permitted it. The key lesson is that the vessel is irrelevant; only the drink's intoxicating nature matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Making nabidh (non-intoxicating date/raisin drink) in four specific vessels: dubba', hantam, muzaffat, naqir. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three hadith: Ibn Abbas on the initial prohibition, Jabir on the later permission when Ansar needed them, and Abu Buraydah on the general principle that vessels do not make things halal or haram.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit permission (fala idha) in Jabir's hadith indicates abrogation. Abu Buraydah's hadith explicitly states vessels are neutral. Thus, the initial prohibition was temporary and removed.
The Hanafi usul principle: naskh (abrogation) is established by a later command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is hold that the prohibition remains makruh. The Hanafi school responds that the later permission overrides the earlier prohibition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that it is entirely permissible. The tarjih is based on the explicit hadith and the principle that only intoxicants are haram.
This is Zahir al-Riwayah, supported by Imam Muhammad's texts.

کے ساتھ ملانے سے (ب) حضور نے روکا برتنوں سے تو انصار نے کہا یہ تو ہمارے لئے ضروری ہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا پھر تو کوئی بات نہیں ہے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا میں تم لوگوں کو برتنوں سے روکا کرتا تھا لیکن برتن نہ کسی چیز کو حلال کرتا ہے اور نہ اس کو حرام کرتا ہے۔ پس قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ہر نشہ آور چیز حرام ہے۔
And there is no harm in making nabidh in gourds, green jars, pitch-covered jars, and hollowed-out wood. There is no objection to making nabidh in the gourd vessel, the green jar, the resin-coated jar, and the carved wood. In the time of ignorance, they used to make wine in these vessels. The characteristic of these vessels is that wine quickly becomes intoxicating. Therefore, when wine was prohibited, they were also prevented from making nabidh in these vessels. Later, when people developed aversion to wine, permission was given to make nabidh in these vessels. The vessel is not the issue; the issue is the wine. So the prohibition of vessels was to change the habit. Later, permission was given to use these vessels. There is a hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade (making nabidh in) gourds, green jars, pitch-covered jars, and hollowed-out wood, and mixing ripe dates with unripe dates. This hadith indicates that making nabidh in the mentioned vessels was prohibited. Later, permission was given. The evidence for this is the hadith: Jabir said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade (using) vessels. The Ansar said: We have no alternative but to use them. He said: Then there is no harm. This hadith shows that making nabidh in gourds etc. is now permissible. The principle: all these issues are based on the principle that if it is intoxicating and causes intoxication, drinking it is not permissible. And if it is not intoxicating and does not cause intoxication, drinking it is permissible. The evidence is the hadith: Abu Buraydah narrated that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: I forbade you from (using certain) vessels, but vessels do not make anything lawful or unlawful. Every intoxicant is forbidden. Ad-dubba': gourd. In ancient times, they would hollow out gourds to make vessels in which they made wine. It is called a gourd vessel. The margin note (continuing from previous page): that two-thirds have been burned and one-third remains. (A) Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet forbade using gourd vessels, red clay jars, pitch-coated vessels, and hollowed wood, and mixing fresh dates with ripening dates. (B) The Prophet forbade vessels, so the Ansar said: We have no need for them. He said: Then it is fine. (C) He said: I used to forbid you from vessels, but vessels do not make anything lawful or unlawful. So the rule is that every intoxicant is forbidden.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of making nabidh (a non-intoxicating date drink) in four specific types of vessels: gourds (dubba'), green glazed jars (hantam), pitch-coated jars (muzaffat), and hollowed-out wood (naqir). The author begins by stating the ruling: there is no harm in using these vessels. He then explains the historical context: during the Jahiliyyah, these vessels were used for wine-making, and because wine quickly becomes intoxicating in them, the Prophet (peace be upon him) initially prohibited making nabidh in them to wean people away from wine. Once the people developed a strong aversion to wine, the prohibition was abrogated and permission granted, since the vessel itself is not what makes something halal or haram. The author supports this with three hadiths: first, Ibn Abbas reports the initial prohibition; second, Jabir reports that when the Ansar expressed need for these vessels, the Prophet permitted them; third, Abu Buraydah reports the general principle that vessels do not render things lawful or unlawful—only intoxication matters. The key legal principle drawn here is that the ruling depends on whether the drink is intoxicating (muskir) or not; vessels are irrelevant. This is a clear example of naskh (abrogation) in action, and the Hanafi position that the later permission abrogates the earlier prohibition, which is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
الدباء (al-dubba'): A gourd vessel made from a hollowed-out gourd used for fermenting drinks.
الحنتم (al-hantam): Green glazed earthenware jars, often used for wine storage.
المزفّت (al-muzaffat): Pitch-coated vessels, sealed with tar to prevent seepage.
النقير (al-naqir): A hollowed-out log or piece of wood used as a container.
الانتباذ (al-intibadh): The process of making nabidh, a non-intoxicating drink from dates or raisins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the underlying principle regarding nabidh made in the four specific vessels (dubba', hantam, muzaffat, naqir)?
A) The vessels are inherently haram, so nabidh in them is forbidden.
B) The vessels are permissible, but the drink must be non-intoxicating.
C) It is makruh to use these vessels for nabidh.
D) The ruling depends on the type of vessel, not the drink.

Key Takeaway
Making nabidh in the four prohibited vessels is permissible as long as the drink is not intoxicating, because the initial prohibition was abrogated and vessels are neutral.

Wine Vinegar and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on wine vinegar and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wine vinegar, explain the Shafi'i opposition, and evaluate the proofs used by each school.

Core Idea
Wine becomes halal vinegar whether naturally or intentionally; the Hanafi school permits what the Shafi'i school considers makruh.

In this lesson, we examine a classic ikhtilaf: the status of wine that turns into vinegar. The Hanafi school permits its consumption even if the transformation was intentional, while Imam al-Shafi'i deems it makruh. The disagreement turns on the interpretation of a hadith and the weight of companion practice (athar).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules on wine that becomes vinegar, both spontaneously and by intentional addition.
The text states: 'And if wine turns into vinegar, it becomes permissible, whether by itself or by something thrown into it. And it is not disliked to intentionally turn it into vinegar.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds both using wine vinegar and making it intentionally as makruh.
Shafi'i's ruling is based on a hadith prohibition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Anas where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'No' when asked about making wine into vinegar.
The hadith is cited in the text to show Shafi'i's evidential basis.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school counters the hadith: the prohibition applies to wine that is still intoxicating, not after it becomes vinegar. They cite the athar of Aisha and the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
The Hanafi response interprets the hadith narrowly and gives precedence to companion practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafi considers wine vinegar halal and its intentional production permissible; Shafi'i considers it makruh, so adherents would avoid it.
The difference affects daily consumption and commercial use of wine vinegar.

[2578] (10) واذا تخلّلت الخمر حلت سواء صارت بنفسها خلا او بشيء طرح فيها [2579] (11) ولا يكره تخليلها. سألت عائشة عن خل الخمر قالت لا بأس به هو ادام (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۳ نو في الخمر مخلل ج خامس ص ۹۸ نمبر ۲۴۰۸۳، مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخمر تجعل خلاج تاسع ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۱۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنادیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شراب کا سرکہ استعمال کرنا یا شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ ہے۔ حدیث میں سرکہ بنانے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ عن انس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الخمر تتخذ خلا؟ فقال لا (مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم تخلیل الخمر ص ۱۶۳ نمبر ۱۹۸۳/ ابو داؤد، باب ما جاء فی الخمر تخلل ص ۱۶۱ نمبر ۳۶۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ [2579] (11) شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ قال شهدت عمر بن عبد العزيز كتب الى عامله بواسط ان لا تحملوا الخمر من قرية الى قرية وما ادرکت فاجعله خلا (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۲۴ فی الخمر تحول خلاج خامس ص ۹۹ نمبر ۲۴۰۹۰ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الخمر يجعل خلا ج تاسع ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۱۷۱۰۹) اس اثر معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ حضرت عمر بن عبد العزیز نے ایسا کرنے کا حکم دیا تھا۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ ہے۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں حضور سے پوچھا کیا شراب کو سرکہ بنالیں؟ تو آپ نے فرمایا نہیں ایسا نہ کرو جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ ہے۔
(10) And if wine turns into vinegar, it becomes permissible, whether it becomes vinegar by itself or by something thrown into it. (11) And it is not disliked to intentionally turn it into vinegar. I asked Aisha about wine vinegar; she said: There is no harm in it; it is a condiment. From this athar it is known that if wine is made into vinegar, eating it is permissible. Imam Shafi'i says: Using wine vinegar or making wine into vinegar is disliked. There is a hadith prohibiting making vinegar: Anas reported that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about wine being made into vinegar; he said: No. From this hadith it is understood that making wine into vinegar is not permissible. (11) Making wine into vinegar is not disliked. There is an athar: I witnessed Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz writing to his governor in Wasit: Do not transport wine from village to village, and whatever you find, make it into vinegar. From this athar it is known that making wine into vinegar is not disliked because Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ordered it. According to Imam Shafi'i, making wine into vinegar is disliked. In the hadith above, the Prophet was asked: Should we make wine into vinegar? He said: No, do not do so, which indicates that making wine into vinegar is disliked.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on wine that turns into vinegar (takhallul). The author presents the Hanafi position in two parts: (10) if wine becomes vinegar, it becomes halal regardless of whether the transformation occurs naturally or by adding a substance; (11) it is not makruh to intentionally cause this transformation. The proof is from the athar of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), who said wine vinegar is permissible and is a condiment. The author then notes the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers both using wine vinegar and intentionally making it makruh. Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith of Anas where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'No' when asked about making wine into vinegar. The Hanafi response counters with the athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, who ordered his governor to turn seized wine into vinegar, indicating that it is not makruh. The Hanafi interpretation of the hadith of Anas is that the prohibition was due to the wine being considered impure or to encourage discarding it, but once it becomes vinegar, the impurity is removed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view: wine vinegar is halal, and intentionally making it is not makruh.

Key Terms
تخلّلت (takhallalat): The process of wine turning into vinegar (acetic acid) through oxidation or addition.
التخليل (al-takhlil): The act of intentionally turning wine into vinegar.
خلا (khallan): Vinegar derived from wine; considered a condiment (idam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on intentionally making wine into vinegar?
A) It is haram because the Prophet prohibited it.
B) It is makruh tanzihan, as per Imam Shafi'i.
C) It is not makruh; it is permissible.
D) It is wajib to turn all wine into vinegar.

Key Takeaway
Wine vinegar is halal in the Hanafi school, whether the transformation is spontaneous or intentional, and the ruling is based on companion practice over a hadith prohibition.

intermediate
6 min
Turning Wine into Vinegar: Halal and Not Disliked
Ruling on wine vinegar with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wine vinegar and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i position, citing the key evidences.

Core Idea
Wine that becomes vinegar is halal, and intentionally making it into vinegar is not makruh—transformation changes the ruling.

In this lesson, we examine a classic inter-madhhab dispute: what happens when wine turns into vinegar? The Hanafi school rules that the transformation purifies the substance, making it lawful to consume and sell, and that intentionally causing the transformation is not disliked. The Shafi'i school considers it makruh based on a prophetic prohibition. Let's explore the evidence and reasoning behind each position, and see how the Hanafi school defends its view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: wine that becomes vinegar is halal, regardless of how it happens (naturally or by adding something). Intentionally making it into vinegar is not makruh.
The text says: 'ولا يكره تخليلها' (and its making into vinegar is not disliked).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds both consuming vinegar from wine and making wine into vinegar to be makruh (disliked).
Shafi'i relies on a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'لا' when asked about making wine into vinegar.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith from Anas: the Prophet was asked about wine being made into vinegar and replied with a negation. Understand why Shafi'i sees this as a prohibition.
The hadith is in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as a recommendation (makruh tanzihi) or a precaution against resembling wine-makers, not an absolute prohibition. They cite stronger evidence: the athar from Aisha and the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
Aisha said: 'لا بأس به هو ادام' (no harm, it is a condiment). Umar ordered his governor to make confiscated wine into vinegar.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says wine vinegar is halal and making it is not disliked (mubah), while Shafi'i says it is makruh. For a Hanafi, there is no sin in consuming or producing it; for a Shafi'i, it is better to avoid.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).

كتاب الاشربة
[۲۷] (۱۰) واذا تخلّلت الخمر حلت سواء صارت بنفسها خلا او بشيء طرح فيها [۲۵۷۹] (۱۱) ولا يكره تخليلها.

سبز اور لال قسم کا منکا ہوتا تھا جس میں شراب بناتے تھے، المزفت : یہ زفت سے مشتق ہے تارکول جیسی ایک چیز جو مٹکوں پر ملتے ہیں، مزفت وہ برتن یا مٹکا جس پر تارکول ملا ہوا ہو ۔ اس میں بھی شراب بناتے تھے، النقیر : نقر سے مشتق ہے کھودنا ، اہل عرب لکڑی کو درمیان سے کھود کر برتن بناتے تھے جس کو فقیر کہتے ہیں۔
[۲۵۷۸] (۱۰) اگر شراب سرکہ بن جائے تو حلال ہے چاہے خود بخود سرکہ بن جائے یا اس میں کوئی چیز ڈالنے سے بنے۔ سألت عائشة عن خل الخمر قالت لا بأس به هو ادام (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیتہ ۳ نو فی الخمر مخلل ج خامس ص ۹۸ نمبر ۲۴۰۸۳ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخمر تجعل خلاج تاسع ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۱۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنادیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شراب کا سرکہ استعمال کرنا یا شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ ہے۔
حدیث میں سرکہ بنانے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ عن انس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الخمر تتخذ خلا؟ فقال لا (ب)(مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم تخلیل الخمر ص ۱۶۳ نمبر ۱۹۸۳/ ابو داؤد، باب ما جاء فی الخمر تخلل ص ۱۶۱ نمبر ۳۶۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔
[۲۵۷۹] (۱۱) شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
اثر میں ہے۔ قال شهدت عمر بن عبد العزيز كتب الى عامله بواسط ان لا تحملوا الخمر من قرية الى قرية وما ادرکت فاجعله خلا (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیتہ ۲۴ فی الخمر تحول خلاج خامس ص ۹۹ نمبر ۲۴۰۹۰ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الخمر يجعل خلا ج تاسع ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۱۷۱۰۹) اس اثر معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنانا مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ حضرت عمر بن عبد العزیز نے ایسا کرنے کا حکم دیا تھا۔
Book of Drinks. [27] (10) And if wine becomes vinegar, it is lawful, whether it becomes vinegar by itself or by something thrown into it. [2579] (11) And its making into vinegar is not disliked. [Urdu:] There were green and red types of grapes from which wine was made. Al-Muzaffat: derived from zift, a tar-like substance applied to pots; a pot coated with tar. Wine was also made in these. An-Naqir: derived from naqar, to hollow out; the Arabs would hollow out wood to make vessels called naqir. [2578] (10) If wine becomes vinegar, it is halal, whether it becomes vinegar by itself or by something added to it. I asked Aisha about vinegar from wine; she said there is no harm, it is a condiment (athar from Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that if wine is made into vinegar, eating it is halal. Imam Shafi'i says that using vinegar from wine or making wine into vinegar is makruh. There is a hadith prohibiting making vinegar: from Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about wine being made into vinegar; he said no (Muslim, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that making wine into vinegar is not permissible. [2579] (11) Making wine into vinegar is not makruh. There is an athar: I witnessed Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz writing to his governor in Wasit that do not transport wine from village to village, and whatever you find, make it into vinegar (Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that making wine into vinegar is not makruh because Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ordered it.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ashriba discusses the ruling on wine that turns into vinegar. The author first states the ruling: if wine becomes vinegar, it becomes halal regardless of whether the transformation occurs naturally or by adding something. Then he rules that intentionally making wine into vinegar is not makruh. The Urdu commentary expands on the types of wine vessels mentioned earlier (muzaffat, naqir) and then provides evidence. The Hanafi position relies on the athar from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said vinegar from wine is permissible as a condiment. The commentator then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers it makruh based on a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade making wine into vinegar. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition in that hadith is not absolute; rather it is a recommendation (tanzihi) to avoid resembling the practice of wine-makers. This is supported by the action of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, who instructed his governor to turn confiscated wine into vinegar. Therefore, according to the Hanafi school, it is not makruh to make wine into vinegar, and the resulting vinegar is halal.

Key Terms
تخلّلت (takhallalat): Wine becomes vinegar through fermentation
تخليل (takhleel): The act of intentionally making wine into vinegar
خلا (khall): Vinegar
خمر (khamr): Wine/intoxicating drink

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to intentionally turn wine into vinegar?
A) Yes, and it is not disliked.
B) Yes, but it is makruh.
C) No, it is haram.
D) It is only allowed if it turns by itself.

Key Takeaway
Wine that becomes vinegar is halal, and intentionally making it into vinegar is not disliked in the Hanafi school, contrary to the Shafi'i view.
